style=\"color:#f6c65b;font-size:13px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.12em;text-transform:uppercase\">Module 2 - Lesson 2.1<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":1,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"44px\",\"fontWeight\":\"900\",\"letterSpacing\":\"-0.04em\"}}} -->\n<h1 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:44px;font-weight:900;letter-spacing:-0.04em\">Why Safety Comes Before Speed<\/h1>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"14px\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;font-size:14px\"><a href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/\" style=\"color:#f6c65b\">Course Home<\/a> | <a href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/\" style=\"color:#f6c65b\">Module 2<\/a><\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"32px\"} --><div style=\"height:32px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"border\":{\"color\":\"#303846\",\"width\":\"1px\",\"radius\":\"20px\"},\"color\":{\"background\":\"#141820\"},\"spacing\":{\"padding\":{\"top\":\"40px\",\"bottom\":\"40px\",\"left\":\"40px\",\"right\":\"40px\"}}},\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group has-border-color has-background\" style=\"border-color:#303846;border-width:1px;border-radius:20px;background-color:#141820;padding:40px\">\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">What You Will Learn<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:list {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"}}} -->\n<ul style=\"color:#c6c8cc\"><li>Why safety is the first professional standard in live event production<\/li><li>The real cost of cutting corners under pressure<\/li><li>Why speed and safety are not opposites<\/li><li>How a safety mindset protects you, your crew, and the production<\/li><\/ul>\n<!-- \/wp:list -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"24px\"} --><div style=\"height:24px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">The Pressure Is Real<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">Live event production runs on deadlines. Doors open at a specific time. The show starts at a specific time. That pressure is real, and it is part of the job. But pressure is also one of the most common contributing factors to accidents on a jobsite. When people rush, they skip steps. When they skip steps, things go wrong.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">Speed Is Not the Enemy of Safety<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">Working safely does not mean working slowly. It means working correctly. A crew that follows proper procedures, communicates clearly, and handles equipment the right way will almost always outperform a crew that cuts corners. Safe crews are efficient crews. Unsafe crews create delays, injuries, and problems that eat far more time than safety procedures ever would.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">The Cost of Cutting Corners<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">A dropped case can damage gear worth thousands of dollars. An improperly secured rigging point can fail during a show. An ignored hazard can injure a crew member or an audience member. None of these outcomes save time. All of them create serious problems. No deadline is worth someone's safety. No shortcut is worth someone's life.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">What a Safety Mindset Actually Looks Like<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">A safety mindset means paying attention to what is happening around you. It means noticing when something looks wrong and saying something. It means following procedures even when you are tired or under pressure. It means asking for help when you are not sure how to do something safely. A stagehand with a safety mindset is an asset on any crew.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">Safety Is a Culture, Not a Checklist<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">The best production environments treat safety as a core part of how they operate, not as a box to check before they get to the real work. When everyone on a crew takes safety seriously, the whole production benefits. When even one person treats it as optional, the risk goes up for everyone. You are entering an industry where the safety culture is built one crew member at a time. Start building it right.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"24px\"} --><div style=\"height:24px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"border\":{\"color\":\"#f6c65b\",\"width\":\"1px\",\"radius\":\"12px\"},\"color\":{\"background\":\"#1a1600\"},\"spacing\":{\"padding\":{\"top\":\"20px\",\"bottom\":\"20px\",\"left\":\"24px\",\"right\":\"24px\"}}},\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group has-border-color has-background\" style=\"border-color:#f6c65b;border-width:1px;border-radius:12px;background-color:#1a1600;padding:20px 24px\">\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f6c65b\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"12px\",\"fontWeight\":\"900\",\"letterSpacing\":\"0.1em\",\"textTransform\":\"uppercase\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f6c65b;font-size:12px;font-weight:900;letter-spacing:0.1em;text-transform:uppercase\">Key Takeaway<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"16px\",\"lineHeight\":\"1.65\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:16px;line-height:1.65\">The pressure to move fast is real. But cutting corners creates accidents and delays that cost far more than safety procedures ever would. Working safely means working correctly. Safe crews are efficient crews. A safety mindset is a professional requirement - not an optional add-on.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"40px\"} --><div style=\"height:40px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:buttons -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-buttons\"><div class=\"wp-block-button\"><a class=\"wp-block-button__link wp-element-button\" href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/lesson-2-2-worker-rights-and-employer-responsibilities\/\" style=\"border-radius:999px;background-color:#f6c65b;color:#101010;font-weight:800\">Next Lesson: Worker Rights and Employer Responsibilities<\/a><\/div><\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:buttons -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->","excerpt":""}}Lesson 2.1 live ✓. Now 2.2 through 2.7:{"data":{"id":328,"status":"publish","type":"page","date":"2026-05-25T23:15:56","modified":"2026-05-25T23:15:56","link":"https:\/\/thecrewblueprint.wpcomstaging.com\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/lesson-2-2-worker-rights-and-employer-responsibilities\/","author":280519757,"parent":326,"menu_order":0,"template":"","featured_media":0,"comment_status":"closed","meta":{"_crdt_document":"","advanced_seo_description":"","jetpack_seo_html_title":"","jetpack_seo_noindex":false,"footnotes":""},"title":"Lesson 2.2: Worker Rights and Employer Responsibilities","content":"<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"background\":\"#0b0d10\"}},\"className\":\"alignfull\",\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group alignfull has-background\" style=\"background-color:#0b0d10;padding-top:60px;padding-bottom:80px;padding-left:24px;padding-right:24px\">\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f6c65b\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"13px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\",\"letterSpacing\":\"0.12em\",\"textTransform\":\"uppercase\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f6c65b;font-size:13px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.12em;text-transform:uppercase\">Module 2 - Lesson 2.2<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":1,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"44px\",\"fontWeight\":\"900\",\"letterSpacing\":\"-0.04em\"}}} -->\n<h1 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:44px;font-weight:900;letter-spacing:-0.04em\">Worker Rights and Employer Responsibilities<\/h1>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"14px\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;font-size:14px\"><a href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/\" style=\"color:#f6c65b\">Course Home<\/a> | <a href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/\" style=\"color:#f6c65b\">Module 2<\/a><\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"32px\"} --><div style=\"height:32px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"border\":{\"color\":\"#303846\",\"width\":\"1px\",\"radius\":\"20px\"},\"color\":{\"background\":\"#141820\"},\"spacing\":{\"padding\":{\"top\":\"40px\",\"bottom\":\"40px\",\"left\":\"40px\",\"right\":\"40px\"}}},\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group has-border-color has-background\" style=\"border-color:#303846;border-width:1px;border-radius:20px;background-color:#141820;padding:40px\">\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">What You Will Learn<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:list {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"}}} -->\n<ul style=\"color:#c6c8cc\"><li>Your fundamental rights as a worker on a live event jobsite<\/li><li>What employers and supervisors are legally and professionally required to provide<\/li><li>The right to refuse unsafe work - and how to exercise it correctly<\/li><li>Why knowing your rights makes you a more confident and protected worker<\/li><\/ul>\n<!-- \/wp:list -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"24px\"} --><div style=\"height:24px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">You Have Rights on the Jobsite<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">Whether you are a union member or a non-union independent contractor, you have rights as a worker. These rights exist to protect you from unsafe working conditions, exploitation, and retaliation. Knowing what they are is not about being difficult. It is about being informed.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"22px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:22px;font-weight:800\">The Right to a Safe Workplace<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">Under OSHA regulations, every worker in the United States has the right to a workplace that is free from recognized hazards that are causing or likely to cause death or serious physical harm. This applies to live event production. It applies to arenas, festivals, convention centers, and every other venue where stagehands work.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">Employers are required to provide a safe working environment, proper training for the tasks being performed, appropriate personal protective equipment when required, and clear procedures for identifying and addressing hazards.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"22px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:22px;font-weight:800\">The Right to Know<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">You have the right to know about the hazards in your workplace. If you are working with or around chemicals, heavy equipment, electrical systems, or overhead loads, you have the right to information about those hazards. You have the right to see safety data sheets, receive safety briefings, and ask questions about the work you are being asked to perform.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"22px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:22px;font-weight:800\">The Right to Refuse Unsafe Work<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">This is one of the most important rights a worker has, and one of the most misunderstood. You have the right to refuse work that you reasonably believe poses an imminent danger of death or serious injury. This is not the same as refusing work because you do not feel like doing it or because it is difficult. It applies specifically to situations where the risk of serious harm is real and immediate.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">If you believe a task is unsafe, do not just refuse and walk away. Tell your lead or supervisor what you observed and why you believe it is unsafe. Document what you said and when you said it if possible. Ask for the hazard to be corrected before proceeding. Exercise this right calmly, professionally, and through the proper channels.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"22px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:22px;font-weight:800\">The Right to Report Without Retaliation<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">You have the right to report safety violations, file an OSHA complaint, or participate in an OSHA inspection without being fired, demoted, or otherwise retaliated against. Retaliation for reporting safety concerns is illegal. If you experience it, it can be reported to OSHA directly.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"22px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:22px;font-weight:800\">What Employers Are Required to Do<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">Employers and labor contractors in the live event industry are required to provide a workplace free from recognized hazards, inform workers of known hazards, provide appropriate safety training, supply required PPE at no cost to the worker, and maintain records of workplace injuries and illnesses. Understanding these obligations helps you recognize when they are not being met.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"24px\"} --><div style=\"height:24px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"border\":{\"color\":\"#f6c65b\",\"width\":\"1px\",\"radius\":\"12px\"},\"color\":{\"background\":\"#1a1600\"},\"spacing\":{\"padding\":{\"top\":\"20px\",\"bottom\":\"20px\",\"left\":\"24px\",\"right\":\"24px\"}}},\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group has-border-color has-background\" style=\"border-color:#f6c65b;border-width:1px;border-radius:12px;background-color:#1a1600;padding:20px 24px\">\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f6c65b\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"12px\",\"fontWeight\":\"900\",\"letterSpacing\":\"0.1em\",\"textTransform\":\"uppercase\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f6c65b;font-size:12px;font-weight:900;letter-spacing:0.1em;text-transform:uppercase\">Key Takeaway<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"16px\",\"lineHeight\":\"1.65\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:16px;line-height:1.65\">You have the right to a safe workplace, the right to know about hazards, the right to refuse genuinely dangerous work, and the right to report violations without retaliation. Employers are legally required to provide safe conditions and proper training. Know your rights. Use them professionally.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"40px\"} --><div style=\"height:40px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:buttons -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-buttons\"><div class=\"wp-block-button\"><a class=\"wp-block-button__link wp-element-button\" href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/lesson-2-3-hazard-risk-and-unsafe-behavior\/\" style=\"border-radius:999px;background-color:#f6c65b;color:#101010;font-weight:800\">Next Lesson: Hazard, Risk, and Unsafe Behavior<\/a><\/div><\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:buttons -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->","excerpt":""}}{"data":{"id":329,"status":"publish","type":"page","date":"2026-05-25T23:16:48","modified":"2026-05-25T23:16:48","link":"https:\/\/thecrewblueprint.wpcomstaging.com\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/lesson-2-3-hazard-risk-and-unsafe-behavior\/","author":280519757,"parent":326,"menu_order":0,"template":"","featured_media":0,"comment_status":"closed","meta":{"_crdt_document":"","advanced_seo_description":"","jetpack_seo_html_title":"","jetpack_seo_noindex":false,"footnotes":""},"title":"Lesson 2.3: Hazard, Risk, and Unsafe Behavior","content":"<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"background\":\"#0b0d10\"}},\"className\":\"alignfull\",\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group alignfull has-background\" style=\"background-color:#0b0d10;padding-top:60px;padding-bottom:80px;padding-left:24px;padding-right:24px\">\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f6c65b\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"13px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\",\"letterSpacing\":\"0.12em\",\"textTransform\":\"uppercase\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f6c65b;font-size:13px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.12em;text-transform:uppercase\">Module 2 - Lesson 2.3<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":1,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"44px\",\"fontWeight\":\"900\",\"letterSpacing\":\"-0.04em\"}}} -->\n<h1 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:44px;font-weight:900;letter-spacing:-0.04em\">Hazard, Risk, and Unsafe Behavior<\/h1>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"14px\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;font-size:14px\"><a href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/\" style=\"color:#f6c65b\">Course Home<\/a> | <a href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/\" style=\"color:#f6c65b\">Module 2<\/a><\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"32px\"} --><div style=\"height:32px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"border\":{\"color\":\"#303846\",\"width\":\"1px\",\"radius\":\"20px\"},\"color\":{\"background\":\"#141820\"},\"spacing\":{\"padding\":{\"top\":\"40px\",\"bottom\":\"40px\",\"left\":\"40px\",\"right\":\"40px\"}}},\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group has-border-color has-background\" style=\"border-color:#303846;border-width:1px;border-radius:20px;background-color:#141820;padding:40px\">\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">What You Will Learn<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:list {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"}}} -->\n<ul style=\"color:#c6c8cc\"><li>The difference between a hazard and a risk<\/li><li>How unsafe behaviors increase the likelihood of injury<\/li><li>Common hazards found on live event jobsites<\/li><li>How to recognize and respond to hazards before they become incidents<\/li><\/ul>\n<!-- \/wp:list -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"24px\"} --><div style=\"height:24px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">Two Terms You Need to Know<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">A <strong style=\"color:#f7f7f2\">hazard<\/strong> is anything that has the potential to cause harm. A coiled cable on the floor is a hazard. An unsecured road case is a hazard. A wet surface near electrical equipment is a hazard. Hazards exist on every jobsite. They are not always avoidable, but they are almost always identifiable.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\"><strong style=\"color:#f7f7f2\">Risk<\/strong> is the likelihood that a hazard will actually cause harm, combined with the severity of that harm. A hazard that is highly likely to cause serious injury represents a high risk. A hazard that is unlikely to cause anything more than a minor inconvenience represents a low risk. Understanding the difference helps you prioritize what needs to be addressed immediately versus what can be managed with awareness.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">Common Hazards on Live Event Jobsites<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\"><strong style=\"color:#f7f7f2\">Overhead work and falling objects.<\/strong> Rigging, lighting, and truss work happens above the floor. Tools, hardware, and equipment can fall. Anyone working below an active overhead work zone is at risk. Hard hats are required in designated areas for this reason.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\"><strong style=\"color:#f7f7f2\">Trips and falls.<\/strong> Cables, cases, equipment, and debris on the floor create trip hazards. Uneven surfaces, poor lighting, and cluttered pathways increase the risk. Keep your work area clean and watch where you are walking.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\"><strong style=\"color:#f7f7f2\">Heavy and moving equipment.<\/strong> Forklifts, scissor lifts, rolling road cases, and large pieces of staging equipment move through busy work areas. Stay aware of your surroundings and give heavy equipment the right of way.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\"><strong style=\"color:#f7f7f2\">Electrical hazards.<\/strong> Temporary power distribution is a constant part of live event production. Damaged cables, improper connections, and wet conditions near electrical equipment all create serious risks. Never work around electrical systems you are not trained and authorized to handle.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\"><strong style=\"color:#f7f7f2\">Manual handling injuries.<\/strong> Lifting, carrying, and pushing heavy loads without proper technique is one of the most common causes of injury in this industry. Use proper lifting mechanics, ask for help when a load is too heavy, and use equipment carts and dollies when available.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">Unsafe Behavior Makes Hazards Worse<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">A hazard is a condition. Unsafe behavior is a choice. Most workplace accidents are not caused by hazards alone. They are caused by hazards combined with unsafe behavior. Running in a crowded work area. Ignoring a spill. Moving a load without checking the path. Skipping a safety step because you have done it a hundred times before. These behaviors turn manageable hazards into actual injuries.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">You cannot always control the hazards on a jobsite. You can always control your behavior around them.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">What to Do When You See a Hazard<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">If you can safely correct it yourself - coiling a cable out of a pathway, securing a case that is rolling - do it. If the hazard is beyond your authority or ability to correct, report it to your lead immediately. Do not assume someone else will handle it. Do not walk past it and hope for the best. Say something.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"24px\"} --><div style=\"height:24px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"border\":{\"color\":\"#f6c65b\",\"width\":\"1px\",\"radius\":\"12px\"},\"color\":{\"background\":\"#1a1600\"},\"spacing\":{\"padding\":{\"top\":\"20px\",\"bottom\":\"20px\",\"left\":\"24px\",\"right\":\"24px\"}}},\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group has-border-color has-background\" style=\"border-color:#f6c65b;border-width:1px;border-radius:12px;background-color:#1a1600;padding:20px 24px\">\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f6c65b\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"12px\",\"fontWeight\":\"900\",\"letterSpacing\":\"0.1em\",\"textTransform\":\"uppercase\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f6c65b;font-size:12px;font-weight:900;letter-spacing:0.1em;text-transform:uppercase\">Key Takeaway<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"16px\",\"lineHeight\":\"1.65\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:16px;line-height:1.65\">A hazard is anything with the potential to cause harm. Risk is the likelihood and severity of that harm occurring. Unsafe behavior turns manageable hazards into real injuries. You cannot always control the hazards on a jobsite. You can always control how you behave around them. See a hazard - fix it or report it.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"40px\"} --><div style=\"height:40px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:buttons -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-buttons\"><div class=\"wp-block-button\"><a class=\"wp-block-button__link wp-element-button\" href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/lesson-2-4-pause-and-get-a-lead\/\" style=\"border-radius:999px;background-color:#f6c65b;color:#101010;font-weight:800\">Next Lesson: Pause and Get a Lead<\/a><\/div><\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:buttons -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->","excerpt":""}}{"data":{"id":330,"status":"publish","type":"page","date":"2026-05-25T23:17:35","modified":"2026-05-25T23:17:35","link":"https:\/\/thecrewblueprint.wpcomstaging.com\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/lesson-2-4-pause-and-get-a-lead\/","author":280519757,"parent":326,"menu_order":0,"template":"","featured_media":0,"comment_status":"closed","meta":{"_crdt_document":"","advanced_seo_description":"","jetpack_seo_html_title":"","jetpack_seo_noindex":false,"footnotes":""},"title":"Lesson 2.4: Pause and Get a Lead","content":"<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"background\":\"#0b0d10\"}},\"className\":\"alignfull\",\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group alignfull has-background\" style=\"background-color:#0b0d10;padding-top:60px;padding-bottom:80px;padding-left:24px;padding-right:24px\">\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f6c65b\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"13px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\",\"letterSpacing\":\"0.12em\",\"textTransform\":\"uppercase\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f6c65b;font-size:13px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.12em;text-transform:uppercase\">Module 2 - Lesson 2.4<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":1,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"44px\",\"fontWeight\":\"900\",\"letterSpacing\":\"-0.04em\"}}} -->\n<h1 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:44px;font-weight:900;letter-spacing:-0.04em\">Pause and Get a Lead<\/h1>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"14px\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;font-size:14px\"><a href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/\" style=\"color:#f6c65b\">Course Home<\/a> | <a href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/\" style=\"color:#f6c65b\">Module 2<\/a><\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"32px\"} --><div style=\"height:32px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"border\":{\"color\":\"#303846\",\"width\":\"1px\",\"radius\":\"20px\"},\"color\":{\"background\":\"#141820\"},\"spacing\":{\"padding\":{\"top\":\"40px\",\"bottom\":\"40px\",\"left\":\"40px\",\"right\":\"40px\"}}},\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group has-border-color has-background\" style=\"border-color:#303846;border-width:1px;border-radius:20px;background-color:#141820;padding:40px\">\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">What You Will Learn<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:list {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"}}} -->\n<ul style=\"color:#c6c8cc\"><li>Why stopping and getting a lead is the right move when something seems wrong<\/li><li>The situations that require you to pause before proceeding<\/li><li>Why guessing is more dangerous than asking<\/li><li>How to communicate a concern to your lead quickly and professionally<\/li><\/ul>\n<!-- \/wp:list -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"24px\"} --><div style=\"height:24px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">Three Words That Can Prevent a Serious Injury<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">Pause. Get a lead.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">That is the entire lesson. But because it is easy to say and hard to actually do under pressure, it is worth understanding why it matters and when it applies.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">When to Pause<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">You should pause and get a lead any time you are about to do something and you are not completely sure it is safe or correct. This includes situations where something looks different than you expected. Where the instructions were unclear or incomplete. Where the equipment does not look right. Where the environment has changed since you received your instructions. Where your gut is telling you something is off.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">That last one matters. Your instincts are a safety tool. If something feels wrong, it may be wrong. Stop. Find your lead. Describe what you are seeing. Let them assess it. That is exactly what leads are there for.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">Why Guessing Is Never the Right Call<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">In a fast-moving production environment, there is always pressure to keep things moving. That pressure can make guessing feel like the faster option. It almost never is. A guess that turns out to be wrong can result in damaged equipment, a failed structural connection, an electrical fault, or a crew member getting hurt. The time it takes to find your lead and ask a question is almost always less than the time it takes to deal with the consequences of a wrong guess.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">How to Get a Lead Quickly<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">You do not need to deliver a full report. A brief, clear description of the situation is enough. \"Hey, I need a second set of eyes on this before I proceed\" is a complete and professional communication. \"This doesn't look right to me\" is a complete and professional communication. You are not being difficult. You are being responsible.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">This Is a Sign of Competence, Not Weakness<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">New stagehands sometimes worry that asking questions or pausing will make them look unsure or slow. The opposite is true. The crew members who get called back are the ones who know when to stop and verify. Charging ahead when something seems off is not confidence. It is recklessness. Real competence includes knowing the limits of your own certainty.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"24px\"} --><div style=\"height:24px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"border\":{\"color\":\"#f6c65b\",\"width\":\"1px\",\"radius\":\"12px\"},\"color\":{\"background\":\"#1a1600\"},\"spacing\":{\"padding\":{\"top\":\"20px\",\"bottom\":\"20px\",\"left\":\"24px\",\"right\":\"24px\"}}},\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group has-border-color has-background\" style=\"border-color:#f6c65b;border-width:1px;border-radius:12px;background-color:#1a1600;padding:20px 24px\">\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f6c65b\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"12px\",\"fontWeight\":\"900\",\"letterSpacing\":\"0.1em\",\"textTransform\":\"uppercase\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f6c65b;font-size:12px;font-weight:900;letter-spacing:0.1em;text-transform:uppercase\">Key Takeaway<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"16px\",\"lineHeight\":\"1.65\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:16px;line-height:1.65\">When something seems unclear, wrong, or unsafe - pause. Find your lead. Describe what you are seeing. Do not guess. Do not proceed with uncertainty. The time it takes to ask is almost always less than the time it takes to fix a mistake. Pausing when something seems off is a sign of real competence.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"40px\"} --><div style=\"height:40px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:buttons -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-buttons\"><div class=\"wp-block-button\"><a class=\"wp-block-button__link wp-element-button\" href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/lesson-2-5-incident-reporting-and-near-misses\/\" style=\"border-radius:999px;background-color:#f6c65b;color:#101010;font-weight:800\">Next Lesson: Incident Reporting and Near Misses<\/a><\/div><\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:buttons -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->","excerpt":""}}{"data":{"id":331,"status":"publish","type":"page","date":"2026-05-25T23:18:22","modified":"2026-05-25T23:18:22","link":"https:\/\/thecrewblueprint.wpcomstaging.com\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/lesson-2-5-incident-reporting-and-near-misses\/","author":280519757,"parent":326,"menu_order":0,"template":"","featured_media":0,"comment_status":"closed","meta":{"_crdt_document":"","advanced_seo_description":"","jetpack_seo_html_title":"","jetpack_seo_noindex":false,"footnotes":""},"title":"Lesson 2.5: Incident Reporting and Near Misses","content":"<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"background\":\"#0b0d10\"}},\"className\":\"alignfull\",\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group alignfull has-background\" style=\"background-color:#0b0d10;padding-top:60px;padding-bottom:80px;padding-left:24px;padding-right:24px\">\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f6c65b\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"13px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\",\"letterSpacing\":\"0.12em\",\"textTransform\":\"uppercase\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f6c65b;font-size:13px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.12em;text-transform:uppercase\">Module 2 - Lesson 2.5<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":1,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"44px\",\"fontWeight\":\"900\",\"letterSpacing\":\"-0.04em\"}}} -->\n<h1 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:44px;font-weight:900;letter-spacing:-0.04em\">Incident Reporting and Near Misses<\/h1>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"14px\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;font-size:14px\"><a href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/\" style=\"color:#f6c65b\">Course Home<\/a> | <a href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/\" style=\"color:#f6c65b\">Module 2<\/a><\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"32px\"} --><div style=\"height:32px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"border\":{\"color\":\"#303846\",\"width\":\"1px\",\"radius\":\"20px\"},\"color\":{\"background\":\"#141820\"},\"spacing\":{\"padding\":{\"top\":\"40px\",\"bottom\":\"40px\",\"left\":\"40px\",\"right\":\"40px\"}}},\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group has-border-color has-background\" style=\"border-color:#303846;border-width:1px;border-radius:20px;background-color:#141820;padding:40px\">\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">What You Will Learn<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:list {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"}}} -->\n<ul style=\"color:#c6c8cc\"><li>What qualifies as a reportable incident<\/li><li>Why near misses are just as important to report as actual injuries<\/li><li>How to report an incident correctly<\/li><li>Why incident reporting protects you and improves safety for everyone<\/li><\/ul>\n<!-- \/wp:list -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"24px\"} --><div style=\"height:24px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">What Is a Reportable Incident<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">A reportable incident is any event that results in injury, illness, or property damage on the jobsite. This includes injuries that seem minor at the time. A sprained wrist from lifting. A cut from a sharp edge. A bump to the head. These need to be reported. Injuries that seem small can become serious problems later, and if you did not report it at the time, you may lose the ability to file a workers compensation claim.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">What Is a Near Miss<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">A near miss is an event that could have caused injury or damage but did not. A piece of hardware falls from the truss and lands a foot away from a crew member. A road case rolls toward the loading dock and stops just before the edge. Someone trips over a cable and catches themselves before hitting the floor. No one got hurt. That does not mean it should be ignored.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">Near misses are warnings. They are the safety system telling you that something in the environment or in the process needs to be corrected before the next event is not so close. Reporting near misses is one of the most valuable things a crew member can do for the safety of everyone on the site.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">How to Report an Incident<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">Tell your lead or supervisor immediately. Do not wait until the end of the call. Do not try to assess how serious it is on your own. If there is an injury, make sure the person receives appropriate medical attention first. Then report the incident to the appropriate person - your lead, the production manager, or the venue's safety officer depending on the situation.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">When you report, stick to facts. What happened. Where it happened. When it happened. Who was involved. What the conditions were. Do not speculate about who was at fault. Do not minimize what happened. Just describe what you observed accurately and completely.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">Why People Do Not Report - and Why They Should<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">The most common reasons people do not report incidents are: they think it is not serious enough to bother reporting, they are worried about getting themselves or someone else in trouble, or they do not want to slow down the production. None of these are good reasons to stay silent.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">Incident reporting is not about assigning blame. It is about identifying what went wrong and preventing it from happening again. The crew members who report incidents and near misses are the ones who help build safer jobsites for everyone. That is a form of professional responsibility that good crew members take seriously.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"24px\"} --><div style=\"height:24px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"border\":{\"color\":\"#f6c65b\",\"width\":\"1px\",\"radius\":\"12px\"},\"color\":{\"background\":\"#1a1600\"},\"spacing\":{\"padding\":{\"top\":\"20px\",\"bottom\":\"20px\",\"left\":\"24px\",\"right\":\"24px\"}}},\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group has-border-color has-background\" style=\"border-color:#f6c65b;border-width:1px;border-radius:12px;background-color:#1a1600;padding:20px 24px\">\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f6c65b\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"12px\",\"fontWeight\":\"900\",\"letterSpacing\":\"0.1em\",\"textTransform\":\"uppercase\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f6c65b;font-size:12px;font-weight:900;letter-spacing:0.1em;text-transform:uppercase\">Key Takeaway<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"16px\",\"lineHeight\":\"1.65\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:16px;line-height:1.65\">Report every incident and every near miss immediately and accurately. Near misses are warnings that something needs to be fixed before the next event causes actual harm. Incident reporting is not about blame - it is about prevention. Staying silent protects no one.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"40px\"} --><div style=\"height:40px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:buttons -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-buttons\"><div class=\"wp-block-button\"><a class=\"wp-block-button__link wp-element-button\" href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/lesson-2-6-never-pretend-you-know-something\/\" style=\"border-radius:999px;background-color:#f6c65b;color:#101010;font-weight:800\">Next Lesson: Never Pretend You Know Something<\/a><\/div><\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:buttons -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->","excerpt":""}}Last two lessons — 2.6 and 2.7:{"data":{"id":332,"status":"publish","type":"page","date":"2026-05-25T23:19:05","modified":"2026-05-25T23:19:05","link":"https:\/\/thecrewblueprint.wpcomstaging.com\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/lesson-2-6-never-pretend-you-know-something\/","author":280519757,"parent":326,"menu_order":0,"template":"","featured_media":0,"comment_status":"closed","meta":{"_crdt_document":"","advanced_seo_description":"","jetpack_seo_html_title":"","jetpack_seo_noindex":false,"footnotes":""},"title":"Lesson 2.6: Never Pretend You Know Something You Do Not","content":"<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"background\":\"#0b0d10\"}},\"className\":\"alignfull\",\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group alignfull has-background\" style=\"background-color:#0b0d10;padding-top:60px;padding-bottom:80px;padding-left:24px;padding-right:24px\">\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f6c65b\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"13px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\",\"letterSpacing\":\"0.12em\",\"textTransform\":\"uppercase\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f6c65b;font-size:13px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.12em;text-transform:uppercase\">Module 2 - Lesson 2.6<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":1,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"44px\",\"fontWeight\":\"900\",\"letterSpacing\":\"-0.04em\"}}} -->\n<h1 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:44px;font-weight:900;letter-spacing:-0.04em\">Never Pretend You Know Something You Do Not<\/h1>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"14px\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;font-size:14px\"><a href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/\" style=\"color:#f6c65b\">Course Home<\/a> | <a href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/\" style=\"color:#f6c65b\">Module 2<\/a><\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"32px\"} --><div style=\"height:32px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"border\":{\"color\":\"#303846\",\"width\":\"1px\",\"radius\":\"20px\"},\"color\":{\"background\":\"#141820\"},\"spacing\":{\"padding\":{\"top\":\"40px\",\"bottom\":\"40px\",\"left\":\"40px\",\"right\":\"40px\"}}},\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group has-border-color has-background\" style=\"border-color:#303846;border-width:1px;border-radius:20px;background-color:#141820;padding:40px\">\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">What You Will Learn<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:list {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"}}} -->\n<ul style=\"color:#c6c8cc\"><li>Why pretending to know something you do not is a safety hazard<\/li><li>The professional and personal cost of faking competence<\/li><li>How to say you do not know something without damaging your credibility<\/li><li>Why admitting uncertainty is a sign of professionalism, not weakness<\/li><\/ul>\n<!-- \/wp:list -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"24px\"} --><div style=\"height:24px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">This Is a Safety Issue, Not Just a Professional One<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">In many jobs, pretending to know something you do not is just a bad professional habit. In live event production, it can get someone hurt. If you claim to know how to operate a piece of equipment you have never used, connect a power system you do not understand, or perform a rigging task you have not been trained to do, you are not just risking your own safety. You are risking the safety of everyone around you.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">Why People Pretend<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">The reasons are understandable. You want to seem capable. You do not want to be sent home or replaced. You are worried about what the lead or the crew will think of you. You have done something similar before and think you can figure it out. These are human instincts. They are also instincts you need to override in this environment.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">Experienced crew members can almost always tell when someone is faking it. And when something goes wrong because someone pretended to know what they were doing, it damages trust far more than simply saying you did not know something would have.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">What to Say Instead<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">You do not need to explain your entire background or apologize for not knowing something. Simple, direct honesty is enough. \"I have not done this before - can you show me?\" is a complete and professional response. \"I am not sure I have the training for this one\" is a complete and professional response. You are not failing by saying this. You are demonstrating exactly the kind of self-awareness that makes a crew member trustworthy.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":2,\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"26px\",\"fontWeight\":\"800\"}}} -->\n<h2 style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:26px;font-weight:800\">The Long-Term Math<\/h2>\n<!-- \/wp:heading -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#c6c8cc\"},\"typography\":{\"lineHeight\":\"1.75\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#c6c8cc;line-height:1.75\">Every time you admit you do not know something and then learn it correctly, you become a more capable stagehand. Every time you fake it and get away with it, you store a gap in your knowledge that will eventually matter. Every time you fake it and something goes wrong, you damage your reputation, potentially your career, and possibly someone else's safety. The math is clear. Honesty about what you know and do not know is always the better choice.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"24px\"} --><div style=\"height:24px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:group {\"style\":{\"border\":{\"color\":\"#f6c65b\",\"width\":\"1px\",\"radius\":\"12px\"},\"color\":{\"background\":\"#1a1600\"},\"spacing\":{\"padding\":{\"top\":\"20px\",\"bottom\":\"20px\",\"left\":\"24px\",\"right\":\"24px\"}}},\"layout\":{\"type\":\"constrained\"}} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-group has-border-color has-background\" style=\"border-color:#f6c65b;border-width:1px;border-radius:12px;background-color:#1a1600;padding:20px 24px\">\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f6c65b\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"12px\",\"fontWeight\":\"900\",\"letterSpacing\":\"0.1em\",\"textTransform\":\"uppercase\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f6c65b;font-size:12px;font-weight:900;letter-spacing:0.1em;text-transform:uppercase\">Key Takeaway<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"style\":{\"color\":{\"text\":\"#f7f7f2\"},\"typography\":{\"fontSize\":\"16px\",\"lineHeight\":\"1.65\"}}} -->\n<p style=\"color:#f7f7f2;font-size:16px;line-height:1.65\">Pretending to know something you do not is a safety hazard in live event production. It puts you and your crew at risk. Admitting you have not been trained for something is not weakness - it is professionalism. Say so clearly, learn it correctly, and build real competence over time.<\/p>\n<!-- \/wp:paragraph -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->\n<!-- wp:spacer {\"height\":\"40px\"} --><div style=\"height:40px\" aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"wp-block-spacer\"><\/div><!-- \/wp:spacer -->\n<!-- wp:buttons -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-buttons\"><div class=\"wp-block-button\"><a class=\"wp-block-button__link wp-element-button\" href=\"\/general-site\/stagehand-fundamentals\/module-2-safety-mindset-before-skillset\/lesson-2-7-how-to-listen-during-a-safety-briefing\/\" style=\"border-radius:999px;background-color:#f6c65b;color:#101010;font-weight:800\">Next Lesson: How to Listen During a Safety Briefing<\/a><\/div><\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:buttons -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->\n<\/div>\n<!-- \/wp:group -->","excerpt":""}}
